                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous monodispersed hard carbon micro-spherules derived from biomass as a high performance negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Xu, Shuyin; Wu, Xiaoyan; Yu, Juezhi; Wang, Yuesheng; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">71-77</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.  The theor. energy d. of this system is 200 W-h/kg.  These promising properties are believed to be close to the level required for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1jsHJQCoWPrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhY_17BhhywYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSqs7bK&amp;md5=1d0ab49c7539719d3b644ebc28a2d568</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA00106K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, W. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.                 10.1039/C4TA00106K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DDuan%252C%2BW.%2BC.%253B%2BZhu%252C%2BZ.%2BQ.%253B%2BLi%252C%2BH.%253B%2BHu%252C%2BZ.%253B%2BZhang%252C%2BK.%253B%2BCheng%252C%2BF.%2BY.%253B%2BChen%252C%2BJ.%2BJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%2B2014%252C%2B2%252C%2B8668%25E2%2580%25938675%252C%2B&amp;doi=10.1021%2Fjacs.7b12267&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC4TA00106K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3@C core-shell nanocomposites for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duan, Wenchao; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Li, Hao; Hu, Zhe; Zhang, Kai; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8668-8675</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is an attractive cathode material for sodium ion batteries due to its high theor. energy d. and stable three-dimensional (3D) NASICON structure.  A NVP@C core-shell nanocomposite was synthesized through a hydrothermal assisted sol-gel method.  Ascorbic acid and polyethylene glycol 400 (PEG-400) were synergistically used to control the particle growth and provide the surface coating of conductive carbon.  The as-prepd. nanocomposite was composed of a nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 core with a typical size of ∼40 nm and a uniformly amorphous carbon shell with the thickness of a few nanometers.  The electrode performance of the NVP@C core-shell nanocomposite as cathode for sodium ion batteries is studied and compared with that of bare NVP and NVP/C.  Among the samples examd., the NVP@C nanocomposite showed the best cycle life and rate capability.  It rendered an initial capacity of 104.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5 C and 94.9 mA h g-1 at 5 C with a remarkable capacity retention of 96.1% after 700 cycles.  Also, a full cell using the as-prepd. nanocomposite as both the cathode and the anode active material was successfully built, showing a reversible capacity of 90.9 mA h g-1 at 2 C with an output voltage of ∼1.7 V and a specific energy d. of ∼154.5 W h kg-1.  The enhanced electrode performance is attributed to the combination of particle downsizing and carbon coating, which can favor the migration of both electrons and ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-MXnruCyFELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhY_17BhhywYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXosVWqtLw%253D&amp;md5=d86081db0910b2756c626f1f1abf470d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201206854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and electrochemical properties of P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Guoqiang; Wen, Lei; Li, Yue; Kou, Yulong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The pure phase P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 was synthesized by a solid reaction process.  The optimum calcination temp. was 850 °C.  The as-prepd. product delivered a capacity of 158 mAh g-1 in the voltage range of 2-4.5 V, and there was a phase transition from P2 to O2 at about 4.2 V in the charge process.  The P2 phase exhibited excellent intercalation behavior of Na ions.  The reversible capacity is about 88.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C in the voltage range of 2-4 V at room temp.  At an elevated temp. of 55 °C, it could remain as an excellent capacity retention at low current rates.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Single crystals of trisodium divanadium(III) tris(orthophosphate), Na3V2(PO4)3, were grown from a self-flux in the system Na4P2O7-NaVP2O7.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A novel K-ion battery: hexacyanoferrate(II)/graphite cell</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bie, Xiaofei; Kubota, Kei; Hosaka, Tomooki; Chihara, Kuniko; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4325-4330</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, research on novel and low cost batteries has been widely conducted to realize large-scale energy storage systems.  However, few of the battery systems have delivered performance equal to that of Li-ion batteries.  Herein, we propose non-aq. K-ion batteries by developing hexacyanoferrate(II) compds. (so-called Prussian blue analogs), K1.75Mn[FeII(CN)6]0.93·0.16H2O and K1.64Fe[FeII(CN)6]0.89·0.15H2O, as affordable pos. electrode materials.  In particular, K1.75Mn[FeII(CN)6]0.93·0.16H2O prepd. by a simple pptn. process delivers a high capacity of 141 mA h g-1 at 3.8 V as the av. operating potential, resulting in a comparable energy d. to that of LiCoO2, with excellent cyclability and rate performance in K half-cells.  Operando X-ray diffraction measurements reveal that the excellent electrochem. performance of this material is attributed to its open and flexible framework, which can realize fully reversible K+ extn./insertion and a structural change from monoclinic to tetragonal via cubic phases.  For the first time, we demonstrate an inexpensive high-voltage K-ion full cell with a K1.75Mn[Fe(CN)6]0.93·0.16H2O/graphite configuration to prove its feasibility as a new promising battery system for an environmentally friendly future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr11U4HSf5r7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljdsdcFg7VXXQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXivVKitbc%253D&amp;md5=55eb2e57b3401c9c8548f4e58c5d7f9f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201700410"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T. class="paneContainer"><ul class="rlist tab__content" tabindex="0"><li id="pane-m1" aria-labelledby="pane-m1" class="tab__pane tab__pane-figures active"><figure data-id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Abstract</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#_i1"><img class="rightTab-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/medium/ja-2017-12267f_0006.gif" alt="" id="rightTab-tgr1"></a><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/jacs.7b12267&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig1"><img src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/medium/ja-2017-12267f_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0001.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr1" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Configuration and performance of a cell composed of a liquid Na–K anode, a liquid-carbonate Na<sup>+</sup> electrolyte, and a Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode. (a) Schematic of the cell structure. (b) Charge/discharge curves at different cycles. Plots of (c) differential capacity vs voltage; (d) Coulombic efficiency; and (e) cycling stability. The specific capacities were calculated on the basis of the mass of cathode material.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/jacs.7b12267&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig2"><img src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/medium/ja-2017-12267f_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0002.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr2" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Cycled Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode and electrolyte. (a) XRD and (b) EDS patterns of the layered-structured Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode before and after the cycling with a liquid Na–K anode and a NaClO<sub>4</sub> electrolyte. (c) STEM image of cycled electrolyte salt crystallized on a STEM grid and (d) its EDS spectroscopy. (e–g) Elemental mapping of Na, Cl, and O from the selected area in (c).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/jacs.7b12267&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig3"><img src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/medium/ja-2017-12267f_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0003.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr3" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. A liquid Na–K alkali-alloy anode acts as a sodium anode when working with cathodes that only allow Na<sup>+</sup> insertion. (a) Layered-structured Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode. (b) NASICON-structured Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode. Only Na<sup>+</sup> insertion into the cathode host suppresses the K dissolution but promotes the Na dissolution from the liquid Na–K anode. The lattice structures of Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> are illustrated based on their crystallographic parameters in previous reports. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a></p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/jacs.7b12267&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig4"><img src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/medium/ja-2017-12267f_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0004.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr4" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. All cells with a MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub>-based cathode and a Na–K anode transform into potassium batteries regardless of the initial cathodes and electrolytes. (a) For a (−) Na–K|Na<sup>+</sup>|Na<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> (+) cell, it behaves as a sodium battery at the beginning, but progressively transforms into a potassium battery after decades of cycles. The charge/discharge voltage increase with cycling is a sign of this transformation. (b) For a (−) Na–K|K<sup>+</sup>|Na<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> (+) cell, it transforms into a potassium battery just after the first charge. (c) For a (−) Na–K|K<sup>+</sup>|MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> (+) cell, it is a potassium battery at the beginning.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/jacs.7b12267&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig5"><img src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/medium/ja-2017-12267f_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0005.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr5" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. A liquid Na–K alkali-alloy anode acts as a potassium anode when working with a MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub>-based cathode host. (a) With an initial Na<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> cathode, K<sup>+</sup> stripped and is inserted into the cathode, transforming Na<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> into K<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> cathode, the cell reaction transforms from (a) to (b). The major cause of this transformation is the thermodynamic priority of the K<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub>. (b) With an initial K<sub>2</sub>MnFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> cathode and initial K<sup>+</sup> electrolyte, it is always a potassium battery.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/jacs.7b12267/asset/images/large/ja-2017-12267f_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/jacs.7b12267&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></li><li id="pane-m2" aria-labelledby="pane-m2" class="tab__pane tab__pane-references"><div class="refs-header-label"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i14">References</h2></div></div></div><hr></div><p class="rightTab-references-count">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li) metal is an ideal anode material for rechargeable batteries due to its extremely high theor. specific capacity (3860 mA h g-1), low d. (0.59 g cm-3) and the lowest neg. electrochem. potential (-3.040 V vs. the std. hydrogen electrode).  Unfortunately, uncontrollable dendritic Li growth and limited Coulombic efficiency during Li deposition/stripping inherent in these batteries have prevented their practical applications over the past 40 years.  With the emergence of post-Li-ion batteries, safe and efficient operation of Li metal anodes has become an enabling technol. which may det. the fate of several promising candidates for the next generation energy storage systems, including rechargeable Li-air batteries, Li-S batteries, and Li metal batteries which utilize intercalation compds. as cathodes.  In this paper, various factors that affect the morphol. and Coulombic efficiency of Li metal anodes have been analyzed.  Technologies utilized to characterize the morphol. of Li deposition and the results obtained by modeling of Li dendrite growth have also been reviewed. Ever-growing energy needs and depleting fossil-fuel resources demand the pursuit of sustainable energy alternatives, including both renewable energy sources and sustainable storage technologies.  It is therefore essential to incorporate material abundance, eco-efficient synthetic processes and life-cycle anal. into the design of new electrochem. storage systems.  At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.  The authors introduce the notion of sustainability through discussion of the energy and environmental costs of state-of-the-art Li-ion batteries, considering elemental abundance, toxicity, synthetic methods and scalability. The progress in the research and development of high temp. sodium batteries suggests that all-solid-state batteries with inorg. or polymer solid electrolytes are promising power sources for a wide range of applications due to their high thermal stability, reliability, long-cycle life and versatile geometries.  The electrolytes play a fundamental role in terms of current (power) d., the time stability, and the safety of batteries and, as a result, their continuous improvement and innovation are indeed crit. to success.  In fact, inorg. solid electrolytes pave the way for improving the cost-effective development of rechargeable sodium batteries.  This review describes a state-of-the-art overview of most of the Na+ conductors for use as electrolytes in sodium/sulfur and ZEBRA batteries.  The emphasis of this article is on inorg. solid electrolytes, esp., ceramic and glass-ceramic electrolytes as promising alternatives applicable to all solid-state batteries.  As part of a continuous effort to find new materials that operate at room temp. and moderate temps., NASICON electrolytes will also be considered.  Polymer electrolytes based on poly(ethylene oxide) (PEO) are also very suitable for all solid-state batteries.     </div><div class="casAbstract">The effect of low m.p. impurities, such as Na and K, on the properties and microstructure of Al-Li alloys was investigated.  These impurities occurred as discrete lenticular particles along grain boundaries.  In underaged and peak-aged conditions, the impurity particles are liq. and the toughness and ductility of alloys in this condition were improved by lowering the test temp. below the f.p. of the impurity.  In the overaged condition, the Na and K occur as a solid phase and materials in this condition followed the pattern of most Al alloys and show a decrease in Charpy impact toughness as the testing temp. was lowered.  The addn. of Na and K to Al-Li alloys reduced toughness and ductility at room temp. (at ≤476 Na and ≤23 ppm K).  Low m.p. impurities had little effect on the toughness or ductility of high purity Al.  The detrimental effects of Na and K on toughness exist only in alloys contg. substantial amts. of Li or Mg, which break down the relatively harmless solid NaAlSix phase which exists in conventional alloys.                         rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous monodispersed hard carbon micro-spherules derived from biomass as a high performance negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Xu, Shuyin; Wu, Xiaoyan; Yu, Juezhi; Wang, Yuesheng; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.  The theor. energy d. of this system is 200 W-h/kg.  These promising properties are believed to be close to the level required for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1jsHJQCoWPrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_odKNPfcEvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSqs7bK&amp;md5=1d0ab49c7539719d3b644ebc28a2d568</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA00106K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, W.                         rightTab-cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3@C core-shell nanocomposites for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Duan, Wenchao; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Li, Hao; Hu, Zhe; Zhang, Kai; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">23</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8668-8675</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is an attractive cathode material for sodium ion batteries due to its high theor. energy d. and stable three-dimensional (3D) NASICON structure.  A NVP@C core-shell nanocomposite was synthesized through a hydrothermal assisted sol-gel method.  Ascorbic acid and polyethylene glycol 400 (PEG-400) were synergistically used to control the particle growth and provide the surface coating of conductive carbon.  The as-prepd. nanocomposite was composed of a nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 core with a typical size of ∼40 nm and a uniformly amorphous carbon shell with the thickness of a few nanometers.  The electrode performance of the NVP@C core-shell nanocomposite as cathode for sodium ion batteries is studied and compared with that of bare NVP and NVP/C.  Among the samples examd., the NVP@C nanocomposite showed the best cycle life and rate capability.  It rendered an initial capacity of 104.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5 C and 94.9 mA h g-1 at 5 C with a remarkable capacity retention of 96.1% after 700 cycles.  Also, a full cell using the as-prepd. nanocomposite as both the cathode and the anode active material was successfully built, showing a reversible capacity of 90.9 mA h g-1 at 2 C with an output voltage of ∼1.7 V and a specific energy d. of ∼154.5 W h kg-1.  The enhanced electrode performance is attributed to the combination of particle downsizing and carbon coating, which can favor the migration of both electrons and ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-MXnruCyFELVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhA1UECXuIlNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXosVWqtLw%253D&amp;md5=d86081db0910b2756c626f1f1abf470d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201206854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The pure phase P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 was synthesized by a solid reaction process.  The optimum calcination temp. was 850 °C.  The as-prepd. product delivered a capacity of 158 mAh g-1 in the voltage range of 2-4.5 V, and there was a phase transition from P2 to O2 at about 4.2 V in the charge process.  The P2 phase exhibited excellent intercalation behavior of Na ions.  The reversible capacity is about 88.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C in the voltage range of 2-4 V at room temp.  At an elevated temp. of 55 °C, it could remain as an excellent capacity retention at low current rates.  The P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 is a potential cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqczD0Elkj2CrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhA1UECXuIlNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1ahtLzP&amp;md5=40e819d5a0148ff47a1c864a5d36a054</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201602202"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, L. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y. G.</span></span> <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>55</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">7445</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7449</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.201602202</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1107/S1600536810002801"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zatovsky, I. V.</span></span> <i>Acta Crystallogr., Sect. E: Struct. Rep. Online</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>66</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">I12</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">U194</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1107/S1600536810002801</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zatovsky, Igor V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Acta Crystallographica, Section E: Structure Reports Online</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">66</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">i12, Si12/1-Si12/8</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACSEBH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1600-5368</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">International Union of Crystallography</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single crystals of trisodium divanadium(III) tris(orthophosphate), Na3V2(PO4)3, were grown from a self-flux in the system Na4P2O7-NaVP2O7.  Na3V2(PO4)3 belongs to the family of NASICON-related structures and is built up from isolated [VO6] octahedra (3. symmetry) and [PO4] tetrahedra (.2 symmetry) interlinked via corners to establish the framework anion [V2(PO4)3]3-.  The 2 independent Na+ cations are partially occupied [site-occupancy factors = 0.805(18) and 0.731(7)] and are located in channels with 2 different O environments, viz 6-fold coordination for the 1st (‾3. symmetry) and 8-fold for the 2nd (.2 symmetry) Na+ cation.  Crystallog. data are given.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2PsHPApQOirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhA1UECXuIlNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhsFerurg%253D&amp;md5=b8d6466f5d4a0ca5de0d506a923c9e99</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1246/bcsj.47.813"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuura, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Umemoto, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takeuchi, Z.</span></span> <i>Bull. Chem. Soc. Jpn.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1974</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>47</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">813</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">817</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1246/bcsj.47.813</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Henkelman, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J. B.</span></span> <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>137</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2658</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2664</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja512383b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00220C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bie, X. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hosaka, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chihara, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4325</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4330</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA00220C</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A novel K-ion battery: hexacyanoferrate(II)/graphite cell</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bie, Xiaofei; Kubota, Kei; Hosaka, Tomooki; Chihara, Kuniko; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4325-4330</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, research on novel and low cost batteries has been widely conducted to realize large-scale energy storage systems.  However, few of the battery systems have delivered performance equal to that of Li-ion batteries.  Herein, we propose non-aq. K-ion batteries by developing hexacyanoferrate(II) compds. (so-called Prussian blue analogs), K1.75Mn[FeII(CN)6]0.93·0.16H2O and K1.64Fe[FeII(CN)6]0.89·0.15H2O, as affordable pos. electrode materials.  In particular, K1.75Mn[FeII(CN)6]0.93·0.16H2O prepd. by a simple pptn. process delivers a high capacity of 141 mA h g-1 at 3.8 V as the av. operating potential, resulting in a comparable energy d. to that of LiCoO2, with excellent cyclability and rate performance in K half-cells.  Operando X-ray diffraction measurements reveal that the excellent electrochem. performance of this material is attributed to its open and flexible framework, which can realize fully reversible K+ extn./insertion and a structural change from monoclinic to tetragonal via cubic phases.  For the first time, we demonstrate an inexpensive high-voltage K-ion full cell with a K1.75Mn[Fe(CN)6]0.93·0.16H2O/graphite configuration to prove its feasibility as a new promising battery system for an environmentally friendly future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr11U4HSf5r7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhA1UECXuIlNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXivVKitbc%253D&amp;md5=55eb2e57b3401c9c8548f4e58c5d7f9f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201700410"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T. R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J.                 10.1002/celc.201700410</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                10.1021/jp4078689</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        <script nonce="90f6f001684f775c-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="90f6f001684f775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6f001684f775c-SJC">
var currentJournal = "Journal of the American Chemical Society";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

    });
});
